In addition to an ^cnrican. officer guide, the party was also accompanied

Ibsj but was in far better physical condition than the average of his fellow pri-
soners (due to his having boon in this camp only 2 months).

History of tho Camp8 It was founded when the Nasi Party first came into
power in 1933. and has been in continuous operation ever since - although its
largest populations date from the beginning of the present war. U.S. armor over-
ran the general area in which the camp is located on 12 April. Its S3 guards had
f decamped by the evening of 11 April. So n .. . ... du - -rsoane 1 and supplies
I reached the camp on "Friday the 13th" of ..pnil -nr .d-letter day for the surviv-

Miscellaneous
Character of Durvivinjv Fopulatjon: Males only, including 1,000 boys
under 14 years old. lutellign obia and "leadership" personnel from all of Europe;
anyone and everyone of outstanding intell.ctnal or losral qualifications, or of
"democratic" or anti-Nazi inclinations CE THEIR	For instance, as to
the French inmates, they included 4 anti-Vichy leu.tors cf parliament; professors
of Pasteur Institute, University of Laris, University of Caen, etc; 8 high-ranking
anti-Vichy French generals (including Gen. Vermeau who was at one time C. of S.),
and the son of one of them; and French engineers, lawyers, editors and other pro-
fessional men of the higher brackets, j. particular inclination for incarcerating
> prominent Jews was manifest, there being 4,000 of them among the 20,000 survivors
(these are inclusive in the nationalities listed in the preceding paragraph).
Jews were given even worse treatment than the others. For instance, no Jew was
I ever "promoted" from the "Little Camp" (see below). A few inmates were from time
to time ransomed by their families by personal payments to 33 officers and
liberated to spread the word, among other leadership or intellectual anti-Nazi
personnel throughout Europe, as to the penalties (internment in this camp and
similar ones) for anti-Naziism.
1
/﻿■■■it '
5•	Mission of the Ca:cn; extermination factory. Mere
enough for anti-Nazis. Means of extermination: starvation; co
work, abuse, beatings and tortures, incredibly crowded sleeping
below), and sickness (for instance, typhus rampant in the Camp; and ma
tubercular). By these means man; tens of thousands of the best leader
sonnel of Europe (including german democrats and anti-Nazis) have been extermi-
nated. For instance, 6 of the 8 French generals originally committed to the canp,
and the son of the one of them had died there (and the 2 surviving French generals
appear to be beyond rehabilitation). The recent death rate was about 200 a day.
5*700 had died or been killed in February; 5*900 in March; and about 2,000 in the
first 10 days of April.
The main elements of the installation included the "Little Camp", the
"Regular Barracks", "The hospital", the Medical Experimentation Building, the
Body Disposal Plant, and an .usmr.ition Factory immediately adjacent to this camp
and separated from it only by a . ir. fence.
The "Little Cam". Prison rs here si ept on triple-decked shelves,
each shelf about 12' x 12', lb prisoners to a shelf, the clearance height between
shelves being a little ov^r 2'. Cubage figured out. to about 35 cu ft per -nan;
as against the minirmm for health of 600 cu it prescribed by U.C>. Army Regulations

being "graduated to the 'Regular Barracks'". Duriig this initiation prisoners
were expected to lose about 40 per cent in veight. Tews, hoe ever, seldom if ever
graduated to the Regular Barracks. Carso dije.ieli ury me; suras included transfer-
ring recalcitrant prisoners back to th. "Littl-. C. p".	,.s persons became too
feeble to work, they were also sent back to this c r , cr to the "Hospital".

9*	Medical Exrerimcnt luildinz. Block	^ uat-c ror medical experime;nts
and vivisections, with prisoners ns "guinea pigs". Modicel scientists came from
Berlin periodically to reinforce the experimental staff. In particular, new
toxins and anti-toxins were tried out on prisoners. Few prisoners "who entered
this experimental building ever merged"alive.
10*	The Body Disposal Plant. The design of this installation was a striking
example of "German industrial efficiency". It had a maximum disposal capacity of
about 400 bodies per 10-hour day. All bodies ere reduced to boneash, thus des-
troying all "evidence". ..11 gold or gold-filled teeth were extracted from bodies
before incineration. This plant was entirely enclosed within a high board fence.
No one except the small operating force of SJ personnel was allowed even to look
inside this fence, and no prisoner who passed within it (as a member of a fatigue
party or for any other reason) ever came out alive. Inside this fence was:
(a)	A large front yard on the left;
(b)	A small back yard on the right;
(c)	The incinerator building centrally located between the two yards.﻿of substantial brick construction with cement floors, one stoify,
2" high basement beneath. The main floor contained an Admin of-
_	end, a locker and washroom for SS personnel at the far end, and
--t x^uerator room in the center. The latter contained, in line, 2 batteries of
3 ire-brick incinerators each, each incinerator having a capacity of 3 bodies; or
a total charge of 18 bodies. 15 to 20 minuses were required for the incineration
o a charge. The floor of each incinerator consisted of a coarse grate through
which the day's accumulation of boneash //as extracted at the end of operation. The
fire came from a furnace room occupying tine rear two-thirds of the basement, the
flames being deflected downwards onto the tcdies by baffleplates in the roofs of
the furnace. The front end of the basement was occupied by the Strangulation Room.
The method of collecting bodies was as follows: Roll call was held every
evening, outdoors outside the dormitory buildings. Internees y/ere required to
strip, and bring to roll call, the naked bodies of all comrades who had died dur-
ing the previous 24 hours, .after roll call a aotor truck drove around the camp,
picked up the bodies, and was driven into the fiontyard cf the incinerator plant
to await the next day's operation. But this was 'not the onlj/ source of bodies,
mnaciated prisoners who "had been around long enough", who committed infractions
of discipline, or who "knew too much", or who refused to be broken in mind, were
arbitrarily condemned to death. For instance, in the "Little Camp" where prisoners
slept 16 on a shelf, an infraction of discipline (end particularly an attempt to
escape) not infrequently resulted in all lo being condemned. Luch persons were im-
mediately marched on foot to a small door into ths fence cf the backyard, at a
point immediately adjacent to the right Imnd fronu corner of the incinerator build-
ing, This door opened inwards until it hit i doca top which held it in a position
parallel to the building's ."all - thus crrati.g a corridor about 4r wide and 31
deep. At the far end was an opening about 4' x 4' flush with the ground, the head
of a concrete shaft about 13' deep, the bottom fl :r of which was a continuation
of the concrete floor of the room at the ::	: c of the base :cnt. The condemned
prisoners, on being hurried and pushed t .	door in the fence, inevitably
ell into this shalt and crashed 13* do.,.i - the cc >ert cellar floor. This room,
n the floor at one end of which they now found themselves, was the Strangling
oom. As they hit the floor tney r/ero "airt d, ■ ith a short ^double-ended noose,
5 big 83 guards; and hung on hooks along t; • d rail, about 6-1/2' above the
* -htr-rot; of hooks being 45 ia nr -L_r. >• . consignment had been all hung'
s P, any who were still struggling were stun.. ■ . : c wooden mallet (the mallet
id a noose ai'e being held by Cosnaandant L'.	The bodies were left on the
hooks until called foi by tiic* incinerator cr<.w, An uloctric elevatoi-, with an es-
timated capacity of 18 bodies, ran u t«. tiie incinc-Ji.tor room, which was directly
above the Strangling Room, The day's quota of appro: inately 200 bodies were made
up of from 120 to 140 prisoners who had died ( x.stly in the "hospital", the
"Medical Experiment Building", or the "Little Cc 43"), cud of from 60 to 80 sup-
plied by the Strangling Room.
For a period of about ten days in .•lurch the coal supply for the incinera-
tor^ran out. Awaiting the arrival of a new supply, bodies to the number of about
t ,8C;0 wry ll'i-eweaKko collect in the front yard, stacked up like cord-wood. To
uunoynnCG of the SS this over-crowded the yard with undisposed of "evidence";
and a spell of warm weather created a Sanitary problem. Moreover, burial was a
good deal more troublesome than incineration; and was out of the customary routine.
But something had to be dene. So a truck detachment, and ; fatigue detail of in-
ternees, was organized. The bodies were leaded in he trucks and hauled out of
camp. The fatigue detail dug one huge burial pit, chrew the bodies into it fill-
ing it except for one end, and.covered the bodies. Then the SS shot all the mem-
bers of the fatigue detail, threw their bodies into the vacant end, and covered
them up.
\
Shortly afterwards a new supply of coal having been .received, the pro-
cess of incineration vras resumed. This process was so abruptly interrupted by
the arrival of U.S. armor in the area that the SS had no time to "tidy up", so
that the cycle of operation could be plainly examined and understood. The pre-
vious day's quota of upwards of 120 corpses of prisoners who had died in camp
were parked in a truck in the front yard. The incinerator furnace grates had not
yet been cleared of unconsu.ned hipbone joints and parts of skulls. In addition.﻿the bodies of about 40 inflates who had died since U.O. arrival, in spite
medical and ration attention, were stacked up like cord-wood against the
the yard. American surgeons stated that the adult corpses weighed on4y.^
lbs, having in practically all cases lost 5°^ to 60% of their normal weiJM,
also having shrunken in height.	, N

PRELIMINARY INFORMATION REPORT
Prisoner: Dr. KIRCHERT, Werner

Ref. No.: S02I/USDIC/PE1

PRELIMINARY INEORMATIOH REPORT
!• PRISONER: DESCRIPTION AND VIT^L STATISTICS.
As Chief Physician at the Buchenvald Concentration Camp,
Br. Werner KIRCHERT is directly resoonsihle for the crimes
perpetrated against its internees, crimes which have now become
infamously classic as the German method of mass liquidation.
That Dr. KIRCHERT had a personal hand in exterminating any in-
dividual or number of individuals is susoected, and the irrefu*
table fact remains that he was the medical officer in charge
of the "welfare" of prisoners at Buchenwald, and as such must
have been fully aware of the treatment accorded the inmates.
The responsibility of his position, therefore, carries with
it the culpability for these crimes.
Werner KIRCHERT, alias KIRCENER, was born on 4 October
1906 in Halle in the province of Saxony, Germany, He is the
only surviving child born to Friedrich KIRCHERT, 75, and Agate
nee TOELKER, 73; one daughter, Margprete nee PRAGER, having
died at the age of 34. KIRCHERT claims to be "gottglaubig"
although he doesn't admit to being a member of any organized
church. He is married to Lotte nee NITTMAN, age 34, and has
two children, Klaus, 6, and Friedrich, 4. His wife and children
are at present residing at Luederitz House in Kempfenhausen
bei Sternberg, Bavaria. The prisoner's last known address was
House 24-B, Kripoen, Kreis Pirna.
Werner KIRCHERT received a very extensive education. His
elementary training emnhasized the religious as well as the
secular. This combined training was obtained in three years
at the Klosterschule in Halle. This was followed ut> with eleven
years at the Gymnasium, where he pursued a strictly classical
course. Uoon graduation from the Gymnasium, he turned to the
sciences at the University of Halle, where he excelled in Chem-
istry and Physiology. After seven years at the University he
emerged as a Doctor of Medicine. He specialized in nervous
diseases.
Dr. KIRCHERT is 5 feet 10 3/^ inches tall, and of slim
stature, weighing only 115 pounds. He has an oval-shaped face,
brown hair, and brown eyes. Prisoner also has a large scar
across the bower left side of his chin.
-1-
SECRET﻿SECRET
II. BRIBE PARTY OR SERVICE HISTORY.
Dr, Werner X1RCH3RT joined the Medical Corps of the Toten-
kopf SS at Franksnberg on 15 June 19^6, as a First Lieutenant.
He chose the S3 in preference to the Wehrmacht because the for-
mer looked much more promising in terns of personal orestige
and lucrative reward. His judgment was proven correct when a
little over a year later he was promoted to the rank of Captain.
From January to April 1937 he served at Bllvangern and Wertenberg,
Germany. In April. 193?> he was designated as second in command
of the Medical Corps at the Dachau Concentration Camp. He was
there until November> 19371 when he was transferred to the
Buchenwald Concentration Camp, where he retrained throughout
1938. It was at Buchenwald that he held the position of Chief
Physician in charge of healfch and rations for the SS troops as
well as the prisoners. It is to be noted that the phrase "in
charge of health" carries a differeirt connotation when applied
to the prisoners than when applied to the SS troops. As Chief
Physician it was he who approved the minimum rations for the
internees and the extent of their physical care. It was he who
was responsible for, if not personally involved in the physiolog-
ical experiments including the sterilization operations oerformed
on the non-Aryan elements of Adolf Hitler's Greater Third Reich.
After 1938 Df • KIRCiIZRT went to Berlin, where he worked as
a civilian in a charity hospital until September, 1939- With
the outbreak of the war he was made second in command of the
Dachau Concentration Crrm, and remained at this oost through
November, 1939- In the oeriod from the end of 1939 until June,
1940, he served in SS military hospitals and at the Gutenberg
SS Training Center. He was drafted into the Second Sanitaets
Company of the Totenkouf Division* end in February, 1941, he
was ororaoted to the rank of Major. KIRCKERT was then returned
to Berlin, where he became the Chief Consulting Specialist on
nervous disorders for SS troons as well as concentration camp
internees. In this cauacity he worked for Brigadier GEHTZEN,
who was the Commanding officer of the Totenkopf Medical Corps
*The SS Division ''Totenkopf" was formed of former guard
units stationed at Various concentration camcs throughout Ger-
many. From June, 1940, to February 1941, this division partici-
pated in the French campaign, and in June, 194l, it was trans-
ferred to the northern sector of the Eastern front, where it
remained for the rest of the war.
SECRET﻿S 1 C E E T
and of the Viaffen SS Medical Corps. By May, 194-1, he became the
adjutant to Reichsgesundheitsfuehrer COHTI and worked with him
until January, 1942. Dr. KISCHERT saw action in Southern Russia
ae Regimental Surgeon with the Viking Division in Eehruary, 1942.
For the next three years he served at the Sanitaetsamt in Berlin,
during which time he was promoted to Lieutenant Colonel (September,
1942). At the height of the German emergency in April, 1945, he
was assigned to the Goetz von Berlichingen Division** and joined
the unit during the fighting for Munich. He was taken prisoner
by American troops at Bad Ischl, Austria on 5 May of this year.
In the prisoner's possession was a certificate, classifying him
as an invalid of the war.
III.	PERSONALITIES ASSOCIATED WITH.
Under preliminary interrogation KIRCHERT revealed the
names of only two other -oeo-ole who were associated with him
at the Buchenwald Concentration Camp. These were Professors
BUHTZ and GBR LAC H.
IV.	TIME, PLACE, SPECIAL RSaSOFS, AID CIRCUMSTANCES OF ARREST.
In September 1945, Dr. Werner KIRCHERT was denounced to
2nd It. Thomas B. C.-iEWS, 101st Inf. Regt., 26th Division, who
immediately contacted the CIC at Enns and transmitted the in-
formation that was confided to him. On the basis of this in-
formation the 430th CIC Detachment located Dr. KIRCHERT in a
Prisoner of War Camp at Enns, Austria, and placed him under
arrest on 13 September 1945. He was confined in the Enns jail,
and on 20 September 1945 he was transferred to this Headquarters
for interrogation.
V.	IHTSIiDSD SCOPE OF INTERROGATION.
The scope of the preliminary and detailed interrogation
is intended to reveal the extent of KIRCHERT1s participation
in tile mistreatment, malnutrition, and extermination of the
inmates of the Buchenwald and Dachau Concentration Camps. It
**The SS Panzer Grenadier Division "Goetz von Berlichingen"
was formed in October, 1943, in western France. After heavy-
losses in the Normandy battles it was refitted and engaged in
eastern France. At the beginning of 1945 the Division was still
on the western front in the Saar area.
-3-
SECRET﻿§ JD c H E I
will also tie attempted to obtain the details of the human ex-
perimentation and medical research that was carried out on these
internees by members of KIRCHEET's staff, and to secure any in-
formation that will lead to the arrest and conviction of these
war criminals.
VI.	SUSPECTED COKHECTIOKS.
In addition tp being directly or indirectly responsible
for, and a party to, the malnutrition, torture, and deaths of
persons politically or racially objectionable to the Nazi Party,
it is suspected that Dr, Werner KIRCHERT was the actual physi-
cian who personally administered the injections that caused the
deaths of internees at Buchenvald and Dachau.
VII.	REQUESTS JOB INPCRMATICN.
All agencies who have request for further information, be-
yond that which was revealed under the above intended scope of
interrogation, should notify this Headquarters. All agencies
who have any information on this prisoner, his activities and
associates, above and beyond the material noted in this pre-
liminary report are requested to forward same to this command
with the least practicable delay.
VUI. RELIABILITY.
The Prisoner fears being classified as a war criminal.
During interrogation he tried to be helpful by talking freely,
but always played innocent. It is considered that the reli-
ability of the information offered is good.
IX. DISPOSITION.
The Subject will be detained at this Headquarters pending
detailed interrogation.
/ JOSEPH M. KOLISCF
Major, Infantry
Commanding

facts are NOT correct.
2.	Artur RICHTER was arrested at HSUCUK on 20.10.45 for
driving a vehicle without an E.S. label. According to I Branch,
he has, since 1934, been sentenced to a total of two years eight
months imprisonment on 11 charges of forgery, fraud and theft. He
was released from his last sentence on 8 Jan 41, but he has pretended
that he spent four years in Buehenwald as a political prisoner (his
car, when he was arrested, was labelled Concentration Camp, Buchen-
wald'). He obtained certain benefits by his false claims.

SUBJECT: Artur RICHTER At No.4 C.I.C.
-------------y------a------
Reference your BAOH/3771l/3l/A(PS. 4) dated 26 Jul 46.,
udiich refers to an undated letter from this branch.
1.	I have examined the petition of Artur RICHTER and the
facts are NOT correct.
2.	Artur RICHTER was arrested at EELKIJk on 20.10.45 for
driving a vehicle without an E.S. label. According to I Branch,
he has, since 1934, been sentenced to a total of two years eight
months imprisonment on 11 charges of forgery, fraud and theft. He
was released from his last sentence on 8 Jan 41, but he has pretended
that he spent four years in Buchenwald as a political prisoner (his
car, when he was arrested, was labelled Concentration Camp, Buehen-
wald'). He obtained certain benefits by his false claims.
3.	It was thought that RICHTER was the same man who
appeared on J.A.G. wanted list, reference 11/3 9-15 Sep 45.
Information was passed to the J.A.G's Office, London, on 25 May
46, to the Yugoslav authorities, #10 were also looking for a RICHTER
and to the U.S. authorities. The Yugoslavs interrogated him and
he is not wanted by then. Neither J.A.G London nor the American
authorities have replied and I am hastening them.
4.	The possibility is that this man RICHTER is the man
shown in the ^plw.C.C. List of Personnel of Concentration Camps
Staffs as having been at MAUTHAUSEN in 1942.

SUBJECT: Ida W3ISLSDER, WEISELBACH.
r
The Soviet authorities have questioned the wife of
Otto Weisleder, Frau Ida Weisleder, of Weiselbaoh, Bismarck_Strasse 1,
(near Erfurt). The following is the result of the questioning.
In December 1933, she married August Amot Weisleder, born
1910, who lived in the town of Wei mar, <*nd with whom she lived _
until 10th October 1945* After this date, Weisleder left for Koln,
taking with him their elder daughter. Regarding the activities
of her husband in -the NSDAP, she stated that he became a member
of the NSDAP in 1932, but held no executive post in the organisat?-^-
He was called up to the Amy in 1939 and served as a signalman
with the Tank Units.
Served in the active Amy, but on which fronts she did not k? j
probably in France. August Amot Weisleder visited Weimar in June
together with his new wife, Lucia Charlotte, of Oppladen, Fichshei e
Strasse No. 10, (near Koln), aid on the 27th November 1945, loft for
the town of Oppladen.
Regarding the service of Weigleder in the S3 Forces, his wif?
does not know anything about this, but it is known to her that he
served from 1932 to 1933 ^ the Death Head Unit No. 1/47 ^ the
town of Weimar, wore the black uniform, and on his cap and buttons
wore the distinguishing marks of the Death Head - skull and oross-bc
About the practical activi-ty of her husband in this Unit, she
knows nothing, nor does she know anything about the service of her
husband in the Concentration Gamp at Buchenwald.
Ida Weisleder also pointed out that fee tried to trace her husband
August Weisleder through the German police but without resulj
where he is at the present moment she does not know.
Further details about Stto Weisleder we have been unable to
obtain.
(Signed) Major General MALKOV.
Dated 28th September 1946
Berlin.

My rear Colleague,
I am able to give you the following
irforraation in the BAUMANN case
On tirie afternoon of 27 Aug 45, Kriminal Direktor BAUMANN was
taken away by Eriminaliat ABSTOSS for an interview with Mil. Gov,
According to tile drive? BAUMANN and ABSTOSS finally drove to HILDEN,
Duesseldorf strasse 217, and according to information given in the issue
of the new "Rheinische Zeiturg'1 dated 12 Sep 45 was interrogated there by
the Nrench War Crimes Investigation Team, . On 28 Aug 45 BAUMANN was
found dead'in his cell. I attach herewith the findings of the doctor
who examined him on 28 Aug 45 at 0840 hrs. According to this the only
wounds found on the man were those caused by hanging with a fine chain.
The doctor speaks of suicide in his report, but gives no grounds to
mpport the theory of suicide.
The corpse was then taken'to one of the local mortuaries and
was re-examined by ihe.Kedizinalrat Dr. .NBJHAUS. I cannot give .any
details of his findings. When the dead man was delivered all his
personal effects were missing such as :
1 gold wedding ring, 1 silver pocket watch vdth gold
watch chain, 2-wallets containing oagh, 1 Post Office
savings book, all his personal papers, 2 pairs of spectacles,
1 fountain pen and also his hsoes.
following a claim made in this connection by Frau BAUMANN and
an investigation of tte local police authorities concerning Capt 0RTLICI7,
some.of the a/m articles we.e returned to Frau BAJMANN. The wedding-ring,
shoes, a li ght summer overcoat a nd a brown hat are still missing. Frau
BAUMANN went to -the house in question in HILDEN, where the a/m team were
still staying but could obtain no information.
I nan hardly believe that BAUMANN?'committed suicide as he was
ft tLi innocent of tbs .men murdered in the shooting incident s both at BURdiOLZ
*	and at LaNDTEHR. According to the issue of the new "Hheinishhe Zelttong"
dated 6 Oct 45 BAUMANN was accused at his interrotation of complicity.
I do not -think this can possibly be correct, as according to statements
shewn my: me by the deceased he was the very man who opposed the murder
of the civilians at LAND.7EER wi ih all the means at his’dijposal, and I know
from many conversations with B AUK ANN tha t he very strongly condemned and
abjured the methods of tb e Gestapo. For this reason he was rejected as
unsuitable by ih e unit in Poland.
cont/,﻿Kriminalrai jOSTOSS who was arrested together with BAIMAIOT
is still alive and is at present in a camp at HBCER. He is the only
person who can give-precise information ontne case.	, .﻿Tr an slation of Coo tor's '3eporA«
Herr Julius BWmW, Horn on 14 Mar 96 was examined
Hy me on 28 Aug 45 at 0840 hr s in the garden of 271	“
strasse.	He was lying on the j^ound and shewed no signs of dxfe.
His heart had stopped heatingand the pupils of his eyes were fixed,
fif Srtis h^d not yet ^t in. Daath was caused by
a fine chain ( suicide). On the neck one could see running sounds
leading back to *e ears on both sides, having been t ir°rjJh®

Am 27.8.1945, naeKmittags, wurde Iriminaldirektor Baumam

regierung abgeholt. Uach Angabe des PIW-Bahrers sind dann Baumann
und Abstoes ansoiiliessind nach Hilden, Dusseldorferstrasse 217,
gefahren und It. Angaben der neuen "Rheinischen Zeitmg" vom
12.9*45 dort von der "French War Grimes Investigation Team" ver-
hdrt worden. Am 53*8.45 soil dann Baumann tot in seiner Zelle
aufgefunden worden sein. Den Befund des Arztes, der ihn am 28.8.
1945 um 8,4o Dhr untersuchte, filge ich in der Anlage bei. Danach
sind bei dem Toten ledaglich Verletzungen festgestellt worden,
die durch Erhingen mit einer dtlnnen Kette eingetreten sein sollen.
Der Arzt spricht in seinem Befund von Selbstmord, gibt aber
keinerlei Tatsachen an, auf Grand deren auf Selbstmord geschlossei
werden kann.
Der Tote 1st dann in einer der hiesigen Leiehenhallen ab-
geliefert worden und ist dort von dem Medizinalrat Dr.Seuhaus
nochmals untersucht worden. Wie dieser Befund ausgefallen ist,
kann ich im einzelnen nicht sagen. Bei der Auslieferung des
Toten fehlten samtliche persdnlichen Sachen, wie
1 goldener Trauring, 1 silbeme Taschenuhr mit goldener
Uhrkette, 2 Brieftaschen mit Bargeld, 1 Postsparbudt,
seine s&mtlichen persdnlichen Papier®, 2 Brillen, 1 Full- J
halter, sowie die aehuhe. .

hat sber nichts in Erfahrung bring®* kSnnen.

STA»JBNT of MSX t.wht^ atol'ISR born 12. 7.02 in Heiligenstein Pfalz:	\
I was eiriployed by che Doctor to the vTaffen S3 in the concentration camp at
Dora. "" iviy was that of male nurse at the hospital and "KalfaJctor" (means
literally 'ii^omer'j it is not certain, however, whether the deponent means
what he says).
I have witnessed the following occurrences in these places; in a cell of the
dimensions 2gm x 2m x 2m there were anything up to 23 prisoners. They
were housed in such cells for many weeks. They could sleep only whilst
standing. Through the beating (anything up to 100 strokes) which the-'
prisoners suffered when they were cross-examined, many had injuries of a
serious nature and especially injuries to the anus and if there was no
ventilation the stink was absolutely deadly. Many prisoners died from
these injuries without hospital treatment. All prisoners had only two
minutes per day to wash and go to the lavatory apd during these two minutes
they were driven and beaten with rubber truncheons all over their bodies.
As rations they received daily 130 grammes of bread and 1 litre of watery soup.
The following people excelled in this cruel treatment of prisoners:
^ S3 Qbersoharfuhrer MAX DBOKBRT from Berlin, height 1.80 metres, dark thick
hair parted on the left-hand side, rouiri full face, blue eyes, forceful
appearance, asthmatic.
J S3 Oberscharfnhrer GUSTAV G-RUMD from Berlin, height 1.65 metres, slim face,
auburn hair getting" bald, hooked nose, grey eyes, penetrating look.
The two above men have killed a great number of people which I cannot define,
by shooting them through the neck,
these
Accessory in the second degree and originator of six murders ana cruelties
, wan the man who was the head of the S.D. Department at Dora, S3 Obersohar-
/ fuhrer ERNST SANDER from Danzig, height 1.?8 - 1.80 metres, slim, black thick
hair, foOncl' face, dark penetrating eyes.
Sandex’ has sent people of all nationalities from the Dora Concentration Camp
to the gallows without any apparent x’eason and he has taken part personally
in the killing of many prisoners by shooting them through the neck
Bergen 28 April 1945
Signed as above MAX LEtIR

Wemer Kabel, Banlc Clerk, bom 15. 3.08 in Bartsoh Province Posen, living in
Berlin Wilmersdorf states:
Oberingenieur BROSSARD from Berlin, 1.80 metres in height, dark hair, fattish
figure, wears spectacles. He was in a colliery of the concentration camp
at DORA, as "Arbeitseins atzleiter'1. He belonged to the S.D. of the works
at Dora. He reported many persona of all nationalities and also civilian
men and women who worked in the colliery, to the Gestapo at Nordhausen,. only
for the one reason that the prisoners made rings and tobacco pouches which
they bartered for food from civilians to avoid being starved to death.
The prisoners thus reported were put into the camp gaol and, after weeks of
torture, were hanged. The civilians were also prosecuted for sabotage
and some of them were shot.
Bergen 28 April 1945	(Signed) Werner Kabel.
I hereby certify that the above is a true translation
of the G-ennan original which is attached and marked "A".
n
Capt
Legal Staff,
21 Army Group.

e﻿REPORT BY INTERROGATOR - Captain P.M. Priestley.

_ Interrogation of Hauptsoharfuhrer Ratal KSEUTZER.
#--------- ;
Reference attached translation of interrogation of the
above named.
I interrogated the above named closely in accordance
with- instructions received from Major G.X.D. Draper and5 in ny
opinion, SMJTSSR is in possession of a considerable amount of
information, but is afraid to commit himself as he is acting as
a witness for the defence at the present BE13SN trial, and is
therefore very anxious not to give himself away in any way.
I think if pressure were brought to bear on the prisoner
it is more than likely that we should obtain more information out
of him.
The Rottenfuhrer KLECSE or KUTSCHDW mentioned in the
attached interrogation is at present also in LUMEBURG- prison.

GENERAL NARRATIVE.
The above named was a guard at Belsen and evacuated from that camp
before the arrival of the British together with other S3 characters to lOTMGAffiE.
The date-of his evacuation was the night of 11/12 April 1945 and it is thought
that he left in company with some of the worst characters in Belsen who left before
the British arrived and were at NEUMGAJKE in the final stages, when the evacuation
took place and the parties were removed to go in the two liners and subsequently
bombed. This man has been seen by Captain Stewart and placed in LUNEBURG Gaol
and requires intense and close examination on the following points:
(i)	all personalities with whom he left BEISM and how the selection was made
as to who should leave the camp and who decided it, and the full details
of that iraove;
(ii)	what personalities arrived at NEUENGAdHE with the subject and whether they
had all come from BEISM:
(Hi)
(iv)
the conditions prevailing at HE0ENGA1IE on his arrival:
all personalities of the HEUH'iG&MB Camp and their activities during tbs'
closing stages prior to the evacuation:
(v)	the move and system of evacuation and what part the subject took in it:
to
(vi)	all information as/the seagoing party of internees and the orders for the,
arrangements and the details for the arrangements:
(vii)	scenes and personalities of the evacuation as seen by the subject:
(viii) his subsequent fate and movements up to capture.
ITOTE FOR MTERROGATOR.
This man should be treated as suspect as one of those who did not wait
for the British to arrive at BELSEN and who is obviously in possession of informa-
tion regarding the conditions both at BEISM and MHENGAMME during the closing
worst stages. It should be arranged that he is transferred from LUiEBiTRC Gaol
when the interrogation has been completed to the nearest Civilian Internment Cairo
and notice to be given to us without fail when this has Veen done.

Military Establisliment PEMEM!iJkDE j

The establishment was charged with the development, construction and testing
of V weapons. In addition to the final assembly of V-2, the actual production
of various individual components was carried out in these workshops. In 194^ > I
was seconded from the \7ehrmacht to this enterprise. At that time, production
was confined to development : the mass production plant was still under
construction, and was only completed in the period 1942 - spring 1943. In May
1943 the first prisoners were brought into the works. They were intended for the
mass production of the V 2 which was then beginning and the, four hundred of them
from BUCHMWALD were quartered in the cellar of the P.l hall, which itself was
equirroed with watch towers and electrified barbed wire. A couple of months later,
during the night of 17/18 Aug 43, the great attack on PEfflMMDE took place.
Approximately eighty percent of the plant was destroyed and the casualties were
terribly high, especially in the TRASSEHHBIDE camp which was filled with foreign
workers, and in the KARLSHAGEN Settlement. I helped in the rescue work. P.l
hall was not sparedj a bomb crashed through the wall and down into the cellar
where the prisoners were quartered with the result that about seventy or eighty
of them were killed. As a result of the destruction of the plant, the
undertaking was evacuated to ITIEDER—SAGHSi'ffiRPEN near NOHDHAUSEN / HARZ,
1 -﻿COPY
- 2 -
MITTEKfERKS G. m. 'b. H,, BEHLItT
Bismarckstrasse Lekhaus, A 4 Aussehuss
Factory at MEDER-SACHSWEHFEN near N0RDHAU3M
Directorate : Generaidirelctor RIGKHEY
Direktor OMkrZKl
Direktor RUDOLF
Direkbor von BOVBRT
Direktor WINKLER
SS - StandartenfUhrer FORISGHN'ER
Ihe plant and land belonged to the WIFO and had been used by them for the
storage of chemical oils, fats etc. In 1943, after the destruction of PEHEmHMDE,
the galleries and buildings were cleaned and prepared for the production of V2.
Personnel consisted of about 75 7° prisoners and the balance oi civilian workers.
With Allied pressure on all fronts ever on the increase, every effort was made
here in Nieder- Sachswerfen to restart the mass production of PenenMnde. There
was no shortage of labour as, in the first place all the prisoner's of Buchenwald
were available and in the second, there were the civilian workmen from bombed
out V2 component factories ( Raxwerke, Wienemeustadt, Friedrichshafen, Linke
Hoffmann Werke, Breslau etc. ). On my arrival at Nieder-Sachswerfen in November
1943j I was again sworn to secrecy and warned that, while I had to work with
prisoners, I was to have with them neither conversation nor any other contacts:
if I did not obey these instructions, I would join the prisoners in their caiirpo
I was warned that I had to deal with the worst and lowest " Anti-socials " and
criminals.
Hy job consisted of time-keeping, keeping the job and stock sheets. For
these functions, I needed about 150 prisoners for two shifts. It was the first
time in my life that I ever had to deal with prisoners and it was quite impossible
for me to meet the schedule and orders of the Board with these half-starved ghosts.
On one occasion, Standartenfiihrer Eforschner and Direktor Sawatzki told me that
if I could not understand how to deal with the prisoners, then I would be shown.
As was inevitable, I was sometimes shown and saw Forschner driving the prisoners
to work pistol in hand.
At the time, the prisoners were quartered in the underground galleries
themselves. There lived about 4,000 prisoners, entirely without fresh air or
light. It was not surprising that on strenuous, heavy labour - transport
machinejry and assembly - they died literally like a lies. In the mo
-	i	., Air'"' ***"﻿- 3 -
Nov ^r, December, January, February 1943 - kh- the daily death rate was 100 - 130 men.
As a result, I never had enough men under me for my job. It was an order of the
board that I should give up weak and sick prisoners who were then put on transportation
work and were replaced by less worn out specimens. The rations were so meagre that
the prisoners were forced by hunger to steal from one another the little they
received. The clothing was so bad that one might have called it rags. There were
practically no washing facilities in the prisoners galleries. Footwear was only to be
found on the feet of " Kapos " and foremen. The prisoners were so filthy and lousey
that they represented a grave potential danger to the whole concern. Finally in
April 1944 every civilian employee including women had to be deloused. It was quite
normal for the vermin to run about on our desks.
In April 1944 the prisoners camp ” Dora " ( Centre building ) was completed.
All the prisoners were brought out of the underground galleries and were quartered
in the hutments.
Camp " Dora " had its own crematorium, so that now dead prisoners were
cremated in their own camp instead of being taken off in trucks to Buchenwald as
hitherto.
In June 1944, I myself was arrested by the SD ( Kriminalkommissar FROSCH j
and was sentenced by court-martial in Potsdam to a five thousand mark fine and tnree
years penal servitude for subversive activity against the Wehmacht and sale of secret
information. ( Case file 234/44 )o The court consisted of Oberstabsrichter GRUNSRT,
one " Kriegsgerichtsrat ", one auxiliary member (Beisitzer ) Oberleutnant SPnRLING-,
lJusseldorf, and a olerk of the court. 4fter five months confinement for
investigation, I arrived in SONDEHHAUSEN / TKur. at camp " Dora ". My prisoner’s
number was No. 102 1 05, Block 141 and later block 23.
As a prisoner I was put Into No 1 Works and was employed in the Jobs Office.
None of my former fellow workers might speak to me. The camp life was so grim
that I can scarcely repeat the acts of cruelty and bestiality to which we prisoners
were subjected. A conspiracy among the prisoners in September 1944 led to the
arrest of nearly 600 prisoners. Thirty of these were publicly hanged during working
hours before the male and' female employees in the galleries. The prisoners had gags
put in their mouths and were tied to a beam in groups of ten. The beam was then
raised with an electric hoist. In a neighbouring gallery, a prisoners' orchestra was
playing lunch-time music.﻿Enlargement of the factory led to the "blasting of new tunnels - a job
which was particularly dangerous and unhealthy. The crematorium was so
overworked that the gratings — I once heard - were burnt through and the fum&o©
had to be repaired. The result of that was that the corpses were simply stacked
up on the road in front of our Block 23 and strewn with lime, there to lie for
several days.
In February 1945, a convoy with 6,OCX) prisoners arrived from Auschwitz
and Rosenau. Fully a third of the prisoners were dead. Of the remaining two
thirds the majority are now dead.
The camp was overcrowded and it was impossible to find oneself space. In
our hall which was set up as a cinema, and in block 23 the most frightful scenes
of cruelty took place. The healthy, the sick and the dying lay there heaped
on one another in their ordure. In the crematorium, bodies were chopped up so
that more could be burnt. But still it did not end; the deathrate still grew
and the mountain of corpses increased, until a funeral pyre was built which
burned for nearly a whole week.
In March 1944, another alleged conspiracy was discovered. The alleged
guilty among whom were camp supervisors 1 and 2, were locked into the bunker.
There was an attenpt to break out and the SS guard was killed. But they did not
succeed in reaching freedom. The bunker commander was the 52 year old
Oberscharfdhrer known as " iron Max " ( eiserne Max " ).
Following the bombarxlment of NOKDHAUSEN ( five kn. away ) we prisoners
were taken in great disorder by rail to BELSM. Many prisoners had to travel
As witnesses to the truth of the above statement

T R A K S L A T I 0 $ .
. evidence of the witnesses,
Jv mk taken on the 3rd Kovember 1945 in the Office of the L.i. Platoon
e lolish Military Centre 1-Jo. 145, by Sgt. Jozef Boron - in the cat
e ill-treatment of Poles by an SS-Rottenfuhrer Franz Teuber.
Stefan Kutianski of the Polish D.P. Camp Ho. 8, at loo A Podbiel-
treet, Hannover, born 1/8/1923 at Ostrowczyk Polny, district Zlo-
czoa, son of Maciej and Anna, Roman Catholic, single, occupation: shoe-|
maker,- states:
On the 3rd November 1945, between 16oo and 17oo hrs., when walkingl
along Podbielski street to the cinema, I recognised,in front of the ci-|
nema,. a German soldier Franz Teuber, who from August 1943, i.e. from
the day of my arrival at the concentration camp "Bora" near Nordhausen,
was a Rottenfiihrer-Assistant Storeman and a Puhrer-in-charge of the
stores which held the deposits given up- by all Poles, Czechs, Frenchmen!
and others. Teuber is a member of the SS, wore an SS uniform, and
during the. whole, t-i i.e. to the 4th April 1945, filled the a/m
posts. I saw during mf stay in that camp that Teuber ill-treated in
a vulgar way loles as well as others, i.e. Frenchmen, Czechs, even
the British, several of whom were in the camp as political suspects.
Teuber used to strike prisoners on the face, kickg& them with his boots
and strike with a cosh. His attitude towards Poles was indescribably 1
bad. He was considered in the camp to be one of the haters of Poles,
and was the terror of the whole camp. His ill-treatment took on va-
rious forms, and was performed on various occasions: during the morning-
ap.d evening roll-calls and at any opportunity that offered itself.
Moreover, Teuber took part in M&gMg the hanging of about 2oo polit-
ical prisoners in the concentration camp "Bora", which took place at
the end of March 1945- Buring that execution there were hanged 5o Poles
5o Frenchmen, 3o Czechs, the rest being Russians. I maintain that Teubej
was an active member of the SS, which he has admitted himself. I point
out that I was not myself beaten up by Teuber, the reason being that I
worked in the boot repair shops, and did not belong to his detachment.
I give as witnesses: Jan Eutianski, Feliks Olszak, ^lojzy Borski - all
from the Polish D.P. Camp No. 8, loo A Podbielski street, Hannover.
I point out that to-day, when Teuber saw me, he tried to escape, which
indicates that he recognised me very well. In the conversation with
him, Teuber stated that in the 3o1 Div. prisoner-of-war camp at Bemerode
there were very many SS-men.
I have given this evidence, and, having read it, I put my sig-
nature .
The Interrogator:
/-/ Jozef Boron, Sgt.
The Witness:
/-/ Stef an Kutianski
Witness Marian Giinther-Samulski, from the Polish D.P.Camp No. 8,
born 21/1/1921 at Ksiaze, district Srem, son of Jozef and Mieczyslawa,
Roman Catholic, single, occupation: student,- confirms to all extent
the evidence given by Stefan Kutianski.

Subject: Pranz Teuber - member of the SS-troots - ill-treatment of-
Poles
To: the Intelligence Officer of the Polish Military Centre l\io.145j
Hannover-Gross Buchholz
On the 3rd Kovember 1945, at 17oo hrs. Mr. Stefan Xutianshi and
Mr. Marian Gunther-Samulski -both from the Polish D.P.Camp Bo.8,
1oo A, Podbielski street, Hannover - brought to the R.P. Office of
the Polish' Military Centre a- German, Franz Teuber,. whom they had re-
cognised as a member of the SS-troops and as a Rottenftihrer in the
concentration camp "Dora" near Bordhausen.	\
It appears from the evidence of the a/m witnesses that Franz
Teuber passed for a fanatical Hitlerite, was the .terror of, the camp,
ill-treated Poles, and other nationals, e.g. Frenchmen, Czechs, Russians
and others who were in this concentration camp. He wees generally con-
sidered to be a hater of Poles.. Moreover, towards the end of March
1f45 he took part in the hanging of about 2oo prisoners, of whom there
were 5o Poles', 5o Frenchmen, 3o Czechs, the rest being Russians.
Franz Teuber - interrogated in the presence of Cpl. Leon Ceglarz,
6 Coy, guard commander - stated that he had belonged to the SS-troops
from July 19.43, and that from August 1943 to^ April 1945 he had acted
as a Rottenfiihrer in the concentration camp "Dora" near -Kordhausen.
He stated also that at /he end of March 1945 he had been present at
the a/m execution by hanging of the 2oo prisoners in that camp. He
had l?ft the concentration camp at the beginning iipril last because
of the successful Russian advance. On the way, during the retreat, he
abandoned the SS-uniform and changed into the uniform of the German
v/ehrmacht.
On his left arm, near the armpit, Teuber has a tattooed sign of
the SS-troops. He has been up to now in the prisoner-of-war camp at
Bemerode, where he stated that he was an "Obergefreiter" (Corporal)'
of the German Wehri^acht. He stated that there were in the Bemerode
camp very many SS-men disguised as soldiers of the German Wehrmacht.
Moreover, Teuber stated that Sturmbannfiihrer Forsohner had been com-
mandant of the concentration camp "Dora", and a	called Bear had
been Fdrschner's assistant.There had also been other SS-men: Haupt-
scharfuhrer Brumm, Oberscharfiihrer Helwig and Oberscharfuhrer Wagner,
who gave orders for the ill-treatment of prisoners in the camp. Teuber
does not know the whereabouts of /he above mentioned SS-men now; he
knows only that Sturmbannfuhrer Forschner was arrested by the British-"
Authorities.
I detained Teuber in the Polish Military Centre, and subsequently
handed him over to the British Military Authorities.
I submit this my report together with the evidence given by the
witnesses Stefan Kutianski and Marian Giinther-Samuls^i as well as with
Teuber’s pass Eo. 157.
2 enclosures.
/-/ Jozef Boron, Sgt.,

TEUBEE.
Extract frora Interrogation Report.
Was called up to a Totenkopf Unit of Waffen SS in the KB at
STUITHOF hear DANZIG. Here he did 8 weeks training. Ihen transferred '
to BUCHENWAID where he was for 2 weeks Guard and then transferred again
to the DOHA KZ near NORDHAUSEN. He was there until April 1945. He
was storeman there except for the last 3 months when he was. in charge
of the personal effects of the Inmates. He says that the only inmates
with which he had anyMiing to do were those who worked in his Store.
The number varied from 12 ~ 15. He denies ever having illtreated.
prisoners, and says,he was in his store from 8 in the morning until
6 in the! evening. He does not know whether the prisoners were' even
counted-in the morning, but the count was he/ld in the evening from 6
to 7 o'clock. He and most of the SS men lived in Barracks outside the
Gamp, and when he left in the evening it may have happened "sometimes
that the Count was just being held, but he had nothing to do with it.
He was one of the first to leave the Camp every evening. He has never
seen any inmate illtrea.ted.during the roll call or in fact at any time.
He maintains that during: the 2 years , he was there he has never seen a
prisoner illtreated by an SS man! Denies ever having illtreated the
prisoners, who worked with him in his store.
Says' he knew nothing about the hanging of the prisoners until he
went out of his store to take his boots to be mended. He had to take
them, oiitside the C mp to the SS Cobbler and if he had waited until h©
left wjork the shop would, have been shut. His store was about 200 -
300 meftres from the square where the Prisoners were being executed,
but neither ,he nor.any of the Prisoners working with him heard any
noise i' and it was impossible to: see through the window because the
B rracks-were in the way.' Oh this particular afternoon he left the
men alone in the store (which was permitted)'while he went to give his
boots in for repaif. He passed beliind the square where the execution
was taking place and saw about 10 SS and SD Officers and about ‘200. -
300 prisoners. Some of the Prisoners themselves helped with the hangin
TEUBER was away for about half an hour and when he came back the
whole thing was over. He never found,out why the hanging had taken
place or how many had been.hung.﻿Third Copy

"A"
A foimer detainee of a Concentration Camp, Czeslaw OSIECZAK, Horn 1 May 45
in POLAND living in a Transit Camp at PALLINGBOSTEL, declares :-
"Prom 1940/45 I was a detainee in different concentration camps in
Germany. I was in 3UCHBWALD and DORA, near NORDHAUSEN* I belonged at the
Camp of DOHA to a Section of Masons and as such was employed at ILFELD.. The
detainees in this Camp were brought there by reasons of all kinds of crimes;
there wore politicians, criminals, and Anti-Social criminals amongst them. j.o
my section belonged a foreman FISCHER 7/ho appeared to-day before the Committee
of Fonaer Detainees at Concentration Camps.
FISCHER accompanied the Section at the Camp of DORA to ILFHffi and^
afterwards the Section remained there. From then I did not definitely belong
to this Section, but I was also employed at ILET3LD and I had the opportunity
of observing how FISCHER beat the detainees, i had often seen FIbGhER beating
and maltreating the detainees with a leather truncheon, or grey stick or with
some kind of instrument used when held in the hand for beating.
He never worried much where he struck the detainees, it made no dinerence
to him what part of their body it was. ,/hen the people ieil to the ground
he went on to kick them until they got to a stage beyond help.	It often
occurred that the maltreated detainees had to be carried to the Eevier where
they died at the end of a few days and 7/ere then sent to the Cranatorium.
FISCHER behaved himself like a brute, and has a number of detainees on his
conscience.
I have not received blows from FISCHER personally because I did not
work with his column. It is impossible that I am mistaken about his
identification. I am prepared to search in order to discover detainees in
the camp at FALLIilGBOSTEL who 7/ere part of FISCHER's column and who received
blows from him. "	, •
(Signed) CZESLA7 0SISC2AK
"A"
There also eppeared Wladislw BARfKIHfICZ former detainee of
Concentration Camps, born 27 Feb 06 in POLAND, living at a Transit ^amp
at FALLINGBOSTBL, who declares :-
"From 1943/45 I was a detainee in various concentration camps. In
the beginning I was in the Camp AUSCHtfITZ and from there I went to the Camp
of DORA. As foreman in the Camp of DORA I was under this FISCHER who is
in arrest to-day before the Committee of Former Detainees.	.
FI33HHR was a brutal man, he beat frequently and maltreated detainees
with all kinds of instrunents which could be used for beating. In truth I
have not received blows fran hira personally because 1 always placed myself
so as to be far fran him at the moment when he approached where the work 'was
being done. I was only three weeks under the command of FISCHER after 7/rich
I 7/as placed in another section. I cannot say the names of the detainees
beaten" by FISCHER. I am going to tiy and discover detainees in the Gamp at
FALLINGSBOSTEL 7/ho have been maltreated by him.	_
It is impossible that I am mistaken about his identification ,
am prepared to declare on oath that FISCHER beat detainees. «

PHTER, Criminal Secretary.
There appeared WILLY 2ISCHER foimer detainee of Concentration Camps
born 19 Deo- 08 in BERLIN at BUCKBBURG, SCIiAmtB.LlPPE, ffilUKERfEG 4, instructed
to tell the truth \Tho declares
«
"In 1943 I completed ray last sentence of a year's imprisonment in the
Arrest Prison at Berlin at SPANDEAUj at the end of this penalty I was sent to
the Concentration Camp at BUCHENifAID. Prom BDCHBNV/ALD I went to DORA and
from there with a Section to ILFELD, Nr. NORDHAUSEN. I Was not sent on account
of my political past but for my criminal sentence.
* In the camp at BUCHEWAID I was an ordinary workman and I was obliged
to do ray work like the other detainees. At DORA I was appointed Foreman. 20
or 25 men belonged to ray Group. These men belonged to various nationalities
and were in the Camp for various crimes. They were politicians, criminals
and Social delinquents. I deny the accusations brought against me to-day
of having maltreated and beating the detainees placed under my orders.
I have heard the witnesses in person who have accused me. I can only
certify that I beat nobody. On the subject of the accusations I cannot
say anything but that it is the question of revenge. "
(Signed) ,/ILLI FISCHER

who declares as follows :-
nI admit that I was Foreman at ILFELD, Section 141 attached to
the Concentration Camp of DORA. I fulfilled this function for nine months
from 19^/45- During that period I had about 20 detainees under ny command
and I admit striking them with a stick.
I admit that I lied in my statement of 17 Aug 45 made before

Czeslaw Osieczak
get. 1.5.1915 in Polen,
wohnhaft z.Zt. ia Durchgangslager Pallingbostel, der erklart :
In der Zeit von 1940 bis 1945 war ich ala KZ Haftling in ver=
schiedenen L&gern Deutschlands. Ich war fn Buchenwald und.Dora
bei Nordhausen. 4	^	'
\ ■ . .
Ich gehdrte im Lager Dora einem Maurerkommando an und, war zeit=
weise in Ikfeld beschaftigt. In diesem Lager waren die Haftlinge
wegen aller mdglichen Delikte untergebracht. Es befanden sich
darunter politische, krirainelle und asoziale.
Diesem Komsaando gehorte als Vorarbeiter der heute auf den EZ
Ausschuss angetroffene E i s c h e r an. Fischer hat anfangs
• das Komiaando aus dem Lager Dora nach Ilfeld begleitet und spater
ist dieses Kosrmando in Ilfeld verblieben. Ich habe allerdings
spater dieses KomBiandO'nicht mehr angehort, war'aber auch In
Ilfeld beschaftigt uhd habe dort die Gelegenheit gehabt, zu
beobachten, wie Fischer die Haf tlinge gescjilagen hat.
Ich habe wiederholt gesehen, dass Fischer die Haf tlinge mit eiruem
Schaufelstiehl, einesi dicken Knuppel-Oder was er sonst an Schlag=
werkzeugen in der Hand hatte, geschlagen und misshandelt hat.
Er hat auch nicht danach hingeseHen, wo er die Haftlinge hin=
schlug, es war ihm ganz gleich, wo er sie hingeschlagen hat.
Wenn die Leute zu Boden fielen, dann hat er sie noch mit den
Fussen getreten, bis sie hilflos am Boden liegen Llieben. Es ist
■dann■wiederholt•vorgekommen, dass-die aisshandelten Haftlinge
ins Revier getragen werden mussten, wii sie nach eihigen1'Tagen
verstorben sind und dann ins Krematorium wanderten.^Firedshe:r
hat sich als eine Bestie dort hervorgetan und hat eine Anzahl
von Haftlinge auf dei G-ewissen.
Ich habe von Fischer keine Schlage bekoaiaen, weil ich auch nicht
in seiner Eolonne gearbeitet habe.
Ein IrrtuM in der Person ist ausgeschlossen. Ich werde versuchen,
im. Lager Fallingbostel Haftlinge zu ermitteln, die mit Fischer
in einer Eolonne waren und die voa ihm auch SchlSge bekosiaen
haben.

II. Zur Sache:
Im Jahre 1943 habe ich aieine letzte Strafe von einem Jahr
Gefangnis is der Strafanstalt Berlin-Spandau verbids st. Im
Anschluss an diese Strafverblissung kaa ich ins KZ Lager nach
Buchenwaldo Von Buchenwald kam ich nach Lora und von dort kam
ich ait einem Koaiaando nach Ikfeld bei Kordhausen. Ich war
nicht wegen politischer Vergehen ins Lager gekoiaaen, sondern
wegen meiner Voi-strafen.
Im Lager Buchenwald war ich gewdhnlicher Arbeiter und habe
meine Arbeiten genau so verrichten mtissen, wie die anderen
Haftlinge auch. In Dora wurde ich zu® Vorarbeiter bestisaat.
Meiner Gruppe gehdrten etwa 20 bis 25 Mann an.Lie Manner gehdr
ten den verschiedensten Nationen an,und waren auch wegen ver=
schiedener ^elikte i® Lager. Es waren politi'sche,kriminelle
und auch asoziale Haftlinge dort.
Dj.d heute gegen mich vor^ebrachten Anschuldigungen, ich hatte
die mir unterstellten Haftlinge.aisshandelt und geschlagen,
muss ich be'streiten. Ich habe selbst aus dem Munde der Zeugen
gehdrt, wie sie mich belastet haben. Ich kann aber nur ver=
sichern, dass ich keinen Menschen geschlagen habe. Zu den Be=
schuldigungen kann ich nur sagen, dass es ein ^acheakt ist.

Hemaovre le 17 aout 1945.
Ii'ansfien detenu de camp de concentration Czeslaw OSIECZAK,
nd le 1.5.1915 en P'ologne, demeurant au camp de passage de
Fallingsbostel, declare :
De 194o I 1945 je me suis trouv6 comme detenu de camp de con-
centration dans diff^rents camps d’Allemagne. J-ai ^4^ ^ Buchen-
wald et & Dora pres Nordhausen.
J’appartenais au camp de Dora & un Commando de magons et dtais
pour cette raison employ^ h Ilefeld. Les detenus Itaient places
dans ce camp pour toutes sortes de d^lits. II y avait parmi eux
des delinquents politiques, criminele/af et sociatcc.
A ce kommando appartenait comme centre-maitre Fischer, rencontre,
aujourd'hui au Comite des detenus du camp de concentration.
Fischer a au dehut accompagne le kommando du camp de Dora &	•*
Ilfeld et plus tard ce kommando est reste h Ilfeld. Je n’ai
ensuite certainement pas appartenu & ce kommando, mais j’etais
aussi employe & Ilfeld et j'ai eu la I'occasion d’ohserver
comment Fischer a frappe les detenus. J'ai vu souvent que Fischer
frappait et maltraiteit les detenus avec un manche de pelle, un
gris baton ou avec un objet quelconque pouvant servir h frapper
qu'il avait a la main. II n'a non plus jamais fait attention
ou il frappait les detenus, il lui etait compietement egal b.
quel endroit. Quand les gens tombaient par terre, il les foulait
encore aux pieds, jusqu'^ ce qu'ils y demeurassent sans secours.
Il est souvent arrive que les detenus maltraites dussent etre
transportes au Revier, ou ils deoedaient au bout de quelques
jours et etaient alors diriges sur le four crematoire . Fischer
s 'est condm.it comme une brute et a un nombre de detenus sur la
conscience.
Je n'ai pas recu de coups.de Fischer parce que je ne travaillais
pas dans sa colonne . Une erreur sur la personne est impossible.
Je vais chercher a decouvrier dans le camp de Fallingbostel des
detenus qui ont fait partie de la colonne de Fischer et qui
ont regu des coups de sa part.
v.g.u.
(signe) Czeslaw Osieczak.
\
Comparait egalement 1'ancien detenu de camp de concentration
11adisiaw BARIKIEWICZ, ne le 27.2.06 en Pologne, demeurant
au camp de passage de Fallingbostel, qui declare:
De 1943 b 1945 je me suis trouve comme detenu dans divers camps
de concentration. D'abord je fus au camp d'Auschwitz et de IS
j'aliais au camp de Dora.
J'ai eu au camp de Dora dans ma colonne comme contre-maitre ,
le Fischer arrete aujourd'hui au Comite des Anciens detenus.
Fischer etait un homme brutal. Il a, & cheque occasion, frappe
et maltraite les detenus avec toutes sortes d'objets pouvant
servir & frapper. Je n'ai b la verite pas regu de coups de sa
part, car je me suis toujomes place de fagon & me trouver loin
de lui au mo^ment ou il venait aux lieux du travail.
Je ne suis re&te que 3 semaines dans le kommandm de Fischer,
j *ai ete ensuite place dans un autre kommando.
Je ne peux dire les noms des detenus frappes par Fischer. Je
vais toutefois m'oecuper de decouvsJir dans le camp de Fallingboste
des detenus ayant ete maltraites par Fischer. Une erreur sur la
personne est impossible. Je peux aussi declarer sous serment
que Fischer a frappe des detenus .
Conforms	. v.g.u.

Bn 1943 j'ai purg^ ma derniere condamnation ^ un an de prison
dans la maison d'arret de Berlin-Spandau. A I'expiration de
oette peime je fus envoys au camp de concentration de Buchen-
wald. Be Buciienwald je vins a Bora et de 1^ avec un kommando h
Ilfeld pr£s Ho^^Biausen. Je ne fus pas envoys au camp pour mon
pass£ politiiiue, mais pour ma condamnation precedents.
Au camp de Buchenwald j'etais un ouvrder ordinaire et j'ai dli
accomplir mon travail comme les autres detenus. A Dora je fus
nomme centre-maitre. 20 h 25 hommes appartenaient & mon groups.
Des hommes appartenaient & differentes nationalites et se
trouvaient au camp pour divers deiits. II y avait 1& des deiin-
q.uants politiques, oriminels et sociaux.
Je nie les accusations formuldes aujourd'hui centre moi d'avoir
maltraite et battu^les detenus places sous mes ordres.
J’ai entendu moiTmeme de la Douche des temoins comment ils
m'ont charge. Je puis settlement certifier que je n'ai frappe
personne. Au sujet des accusations je ne peux dire qu’une chose
il s'agit d’une vengeance,

Halmstedt 8.6.1945
To the Officer in Charge of M. G.
in Helmstedt.
I have to inform you that according to the evidence given by-
Polish -witnesses, JOZEP KOLINSKI and JAN SAGAN in Dahrdorf ( 5 km.from
Oebisfelde] is employed as chief of the M.G. police a German WILLY 1RBIKE.
He was a common criminal (Schwerver treeher J and as such he was kept in the
concentration camp Oehra {N0rdhausen) till the arrival of the Allies .There
./ILLY IBfSIKE was there a Kapo in charge of a group of 150 prisoners.
Kolinski Josef and Sagan Jan were in that group.They stated that Willy Preike
has treated the prisoners in a teastly way.He has beaten to death 12 Poles
wanting to force them to do more work,quite beyend the prisoners capacitiesi'
I have to ask you to make necessary interrogation in order to
punish the suspect.V/itnesses may be interrogated at any time. The protocoil
of their interrogation is in my possession.
G.O.of the Polish Camp Police
(-j 2nd Lt.Niedziela Bugeniusz.﻿

iVAH GRIME ARD/OR ATROCITY REPORT
Name. KLAAS, Heinrich
Place and Date of capture; MAHLWINKEL, 19 Apr 45.
Collecting ca,g;e to whicli evacuated:	Camp No 91.
Date of Interrogation:	18 May 1945.
Reliability of Report:	Good.
a ) Military
Brief summary of Incident:- Nature, Place and Date of Offense:
Subject, an internee of the concentration camp OSTERHAGEN, was made
trustee guard of all foreign prisoners, including Russian, Polish
and other national PW’s. Subject admits having mistreated various
Pi's on his own accord. Subject staged at OSTERHAGEN from Jul 44
until Apr 45.
Other Jitnesses Beside P/ff on when Report is Being Made - Names,
Rank, and Present Whereabouts so far as known:
Name:; WEXSHAAR, Baptist
Present Whereabouts; Former internee at OSTEAHAGEN, at the present
interned at camp No 91. at RECKLINGHAUSEN.﻿♦

The information concerning the following alleged
war crime was submitted to these quarters by
Josef Ulhaas, Criminal Secretary, 89,fieusser
8t, Cologne.
The persons responsible for the crime, through
giving orders reap, carrying them out, are
a)	Breull, former Criminal Commissioner,
88-Obersturmfiihrer and aD-Leiter,filens-
burg, allied to be reinstated with
Cripo in T'lensburg	_
b)	Otto, Crim.aecretary, address unknown
After the airraid on the to’/m of Nordhausen
on 4/4/44 the managements of the firms Mit-
telwerke, Niedersachsenwerke hau fled leaving
their workers, concentration-camp-inmates and
D.Ps, to their fate. The camp inmates had
been left without food. They broke out and
roamed about the damaged town, looking for
food among the ruins.
At the offices of the Cripo Nordhausen, Criminal
Commissioner Breull gave orders to all Cripo
officials to take all camp inmates and fi.Pa,
apprehended in the town, into the nearest
cellar and shoot them, borne days later Breull
apprehended a Pole and brought him to the Cripo

1	1 am direoted by the Judge Advocate General of the Forces to return this
ease which has bean referred her® by the Deputy Judge Advocate General at your
headquarters. For the reasons set out below this case has not yet been
registered with ths United Nations War Crimea Coasaisaioa as a war crime.
2 The Judge Adwcate General has instructed me to convey the following advice
to you regarding tpe case.
3 In this case there is in ray opinion sufficient evidence available which
would Justify the ^.ccussd being charged with cosn-itting a war crime, I m
however bound to point out that the alleged dime was ccatmitted at Kordh&uaen,
which is not, and I understand never has been, in the British Tione, and further
that th* victim was an Eastern national, probably a Pol©, In these circumstance
you may think that this la not a case which should be triad before a British
Military Court, If, however, you consider that the case should be tried before
a British Military Court ,then in ay opinion the appropriate charges would bej-
Ist Charge Against all three acouagd
COMMITTING A WAR CRESS
in that they
2nd Charge
at Nordhausen in or about the month of April 1945 in violation of the laws and
usages of war were concerned in the killing of an. unknown illiad national.
, r'

CGMMITTITJG A WAR CHIMB
in that he

charge of the KR2PG at that place in violation of the laws and usages of war
gave orders to his subordinates that they were to kill the inmates of con-
centration camps being Allied Nationals being found in the said town.
4 The accused BREOLL is in No.1 CIO. The accused MICHEIS is in No. 5 CIC.
The accused OTTO has not yet been located. There is in my opinion no reason
why the trial, if you decide to order it, of BSEULL and MICHELS should be
delayed for this reason.

sign the charge sheet as such in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 4

1945. In the heading of the charge sheet the accused should be described as

were buried en route.

To: J.A.G. War Crimes Section.
Prom: War Crimes investigation Unit,
Subject: BAMBERG Bernard, bom. 29. 9. 1922.
prison. No: 77703®
1) Enclosed please find copy of interrogation and one translation
of the deposition of SIMON, Wilhelm, Unterscharfuehrer at present
in No: 4 C.I.C. SIMON has no knowledge of the fate of BAMBERG,
nor does he remember anyone with that name or Prison No:
2)
A certain SCHLEBUSCH, Ferdinand, Marienthal Str. 42, Hinterhaus, MINSTER,
■who was a prisoner on the transport commanded by SIMON, was interrogated
on 42$. 46,, but was unable to give any information. He states that he
would not be able to remeber the names of any of the people on the
transport or in the camo. He thinks, however, that if he were confronted
with a photograph, he may be able to give some information.
Wilhelm SIMON, has been previously interrogated in connection with
this case by the French War Crimes Investigation Unit at KELDEN.
It appears tot the wife of the above BAMBERE has started inquiries
through the above mission. SIMON states that he was maltreated
during the course of his interrogation at HILDEN, and that he is
still, after the course of several weeks able to show the scars
of his ill-treatment.
H.Q. B.A.O.R.
7. Oct. 1946o
Lt. Col.

Deposition on oath of SIMON Wilhelm - Heinrich, male of AlTliHA
Westphalia, Bungern 8, at present at No 4 GIO, before me Oapt.
H.P. KIN SLEIGH, The Cheshire Kegt, of ,,'ar Grimes Investigation

I Heinrich Wilhelm SIMON have been informed that I am not compelle d
to make a deposition, unless I so desire, I am BMking this depo-
sition voluntarily, no coercion has been execised nor have I been
promessed any reward. I have also been informed that my deposition
may be used in evidence.
I am Heinrich 'Wilhelm SIMON, born at W0PPERTA1 Niberfeld on the
23 Apr 1900, I am of Protestant religion. I left the Protestant
Church in 1935, but have now gone back to the Church as a convinced
believer. I am married and have 5 children aged betweeb 3 and 17
years. I do hot know the present vdiereabouts of my family. I am
a merchant by trade.
I became a member of the NSDAP .in 1932, and at the same time a member
of the. S3.-' I did not occupy any function in the Party. I became
Untercharfiihrer in the S3 in 1935 or 36, I received this promotion
on account of my long membership of the NSBAP. At the end of the
,/ar I was still an Untercharftihrer. I did not belong to any other
section fof the IS.	^
I was called up into the Wehrmacht in 1942, in the Infantry, as I
had served in the previous War I was promoted to Gefreiter shortly
after my oall-up. I was promoted to the rank of Unter Offizier at
the beginning of 1943. On account of my age and of the fact that I
had 5 children I was only used for guard duties, and was in service
at the Wehrmacht Transport Kommandantur. I was transferred to the
Waffen S3 on the 1st Oct 1943- I had to report to the SS Wirtschafts
Haupt Verwaltungs Amt at BERLIN, Shortly after that I was transferred
to the Coneentfettion Gamp of BUCHENwaLD. I was to learn the urbeit
Einsatz Ver.altung. I did not do any guard duties there.
At that time NORDHAUSE®, was a working camp of the Concentration
Gamp of BUGHENWALD, I was transferred to it after having learnt a
short while, this occurred in 1943* Shortly after that NORDH&USEE
became a self centred Concentration Gamp. Mittel Werk G.m.b.H.(Ltd)
was the firm which supplied the work to the NORDHAUSBN Gamp, and I
was serving as liaison agent between the civilian contractors and
the supply of workers. But I was not Arbeits Einsatz Piihrer, this
pos t was occupied by Haupt sturmf SCHWARTZ, and when our camp became
self centred Unter Sturmf KURTZ . This one was relieved at a later
date by Ob Sturmf. SELL. I remained in this job until the end of
March or beginning of April 1945-
tit that time arms which had been manufactured in the Cone Gamp oi
Nfi-.DHaUSEN, especially rockets called TYPHOON which were used ror
Ack Ack, were to be transported to the 3E..2HTESG-wRi'ENER Aaum. Haup
3chari. BU3T4 was responsible ror the prisoners who were doing the*
transport. I was in charge of the catering (Varpflegunga Offr).
Ob It 3C"T. Ur pML., who «’tts an engineer, was responsible for the
transport. I have been told that SCn EUPELIN is being used by the
American Occupation Authorities in the capacity of engineer.﻿* \
2
The transport left 1'IOEBHAUSDH, at the end of March or heginnigg
of april. But it never re«chea its destination. »nen we arrived
at TEAUBSBE it was discovered that there were no possiblities to .
manufacture there, on account there being no electricity, water-
power and other reasons, about 200 or 220 prisoners were left there
at the KBENSB3 Gamp, which was sub camp of the MAUIHAUSKu Gone.
Gamp. This occurred in my absence , because I was on my way with
food.
The transport was made up of80 tracks of material and about 10
trucks for the personnel and the prisoners, technicians were
included. .ie continued towards BISGHBAGH and we still had about
80 prisoners with us when we arrived there. Three prisoners were
left at the Kreis Hospital near VIEEBIIBURG to serve as blood donors.
Hot one prisoner died during the journey, noaa escaped or was missed
in any forcible way.
Our transport left IOHDHAUSSN on the night of the 4th/5th Apr, after
the large sc file Air Attack on IIOHDHAUSBff. After this I never
returned to EOHDHAUSEI. Before today I have never heard of a
transport to AMfitIO, nor do 1 know what AM1HIC means.
After being questioned I explain the followingj- I heard the name
Bernard BAMBBEG for the first time when I was questioned here in
EEGILliIHGHAUSEE by a Breach Officer. I further add that according
to the name BAMBEEG it sounds like a Jewish name, Jewish prisoners
were not used in the Secret Production following an instruction
issued by the Beichs Itthrer of the 3S» and as such he would not
have been in my transport. His xm number 77703 does mean anything
to me.
(Signed) W!H. SIMOH

Justice in Baden Baden, have decided to stop the proceedings taken against
the war criminals hereafter listed and arrested by us, this either because
the nationality of the victims has not been definitely established or the
crimes committed did not relate to French nationals.

1. The Case of Buchenwala is oein6 handed to the Russians by
the Americans. It is not known what stabe has been reached in the
negotiations. Gross Rosen Camp is in the Russian Zone, and is pre
sumanly being dealt with by the Russians.
2.	This office has absolutely no information about the follow-
ing camps' and so is unable to help you. Geographical research,
howeve-r, might suggest a possible responsibility - :
Patborg
Schaunbeide

Wernigerode

Wur teg-.ier sdorf

3.	This office has no case file on the following camps, but
can give information which may help
Lichtefelde:	near Brandenburg. Reported as a P.W. Camp in Feb 44.
Heinkelwerk©: one of the working camps of Neuengamme, a British Case.
Vught (not Vucht): in Holland. The main Dutch Concentration uamp,
the oase is being tried by them.
Treblinka (Not Trzebina): ih Poland, connected with Auschwitz.
Niederhagen: near Rostock so probably a Russian interest.
Ausberg:	in Bavaria, perhaps a worming camp attached to one of the
armament or aircraft factories there: if so.probably,
connected with Dachau, which is an American interest.
Landsberg:	also in Bavaria, perhaps connected with Dachau or
Flossenberg, which are American interests.
Konitz: in Poland.
Melk:	in Austria, so perhaps connected with Mauthausen. It isnot
mnown that there was a Concentration Camp there,
Nen-Sustrum: One of the Emsland Group of Camps.
4.	As regards the other camps mentioned :-
Vechta:	a prison camp run by local Gestapo, . housed.political
prisoners. The case is being investigated jointly by this
office and the Belgians.
Hordhausen: Mittelban and Niedersachswerfen:	these are.different
names for the same camp ,at different stages in its career.
Nordhausen was a dependency of Buchenwald until the end of 43.
After that Nordhausen was a camp of its own. It is
probable that «both' camps are being dealt with by the
Americans.
Natzweiler: The principle Concentration Camp in France: dealt with by
the French.
Riga:	In Russia, so perhaps a Russina interest.
Theresienstadt:	The principle Concentration Camp of Czechoslovakia,
whose authorities are interested in this case.
dealt with by the
/Wewelsburg....﻿2
Wewelsburg: in this zone, near Paderborn. Investigations have not
yet been completed.
Osterrode:	the only file in this connection has been passed to the
Poles (accused Spintig’, |*/iili) .

BRIEF for INVESTIGATION of
NOREHAUSEN (DORA).
1.	The above-mentioned Gamp, which is referred to as either "NORDHAUSEN" Camp
by its location or as "MITTELBAU" or as "DORA", wa3 a concentration camp in the
HARZ Area which supplied labour for the V-weapon-making plants in the neighbourhood.
As far as is known it was originally a dependency of BUCHENV/ALD and then became an
independent camp in 194A. The purpose of the investigation is to find out whether
there were Allied nationals amongst the internees (which is almost a certainty)
and what the percentage of Allied nationals was in relation to the Germans.
2.	To find out who the Gamp Commandant and the more prominent members of his
staff were and if any of them are held in our Zone.
3.	The following clues are available;
(a)	Statement by Rudi KOENIG, of DGRITSDND An den Breuherhofen 26.
His statement wants enlarging upon, as it seems that he has a first-hand and detailed
knowledge of what went on in the Canp.
(b)	Albert PABSHDIEOK.
The above-mentioned was first a member of the SS gear'd and later a prisoner at
the above-named Camp and is at the moment at No. 1 Civilian Internment Camp.
(c)	Interrogate Eaul KHEUTZB?, Hauptscharfuhrer, who is at No. 2 Civilian
Internment Camp, SANDBOSTEL. The interrogation made by Captain Priestley of the
above-named is of little value because this interrogation Was done on a brief for
BELSEN and NEUENGAMME.
(d)	Interrogate KLIT3CH0W (Hauptscharfuhrer), who was last at LUNEBERG
Prison where he was held as a witness for the defence in the Belsen Trial.
I have no doubt that since then he has been returned to one_ of the Civilian
Internment Camps.
(e)	Interrogate the following accused in the Belsen Trial who have been
at NOEDHAIBEN (DORA) before thay came to BELSEN: -
Mil Gov Public Safety, who were charged with the disposal of the accused after trial,
will no doubt be able to say in which prison these men are to be found at the moment.

BUCHEMWALD Concentration Camp
Ref. '"your BAOI^/3796/79/A(PS4) dated 12 Dec 46
^ cj3-
^	You^starte in para. 2 of your minute, "It is now established
that the USSR have taken over this case from the US War Crimes Group, and
will be dealing with BUCHEMWALD completely”, while in point of fact, the
reverse seems to be happening. The American Prosecution Staff is over-
hauling and preparing the case for trial at a date not yet fixed, out should
be sometime in February.
2.	Apparently the USSR and the US came together on this case
in October 1945, when the entire case was offered to tl^e USSR. The next
thirteen months were spent in fruitless negociations and when, in Nov
1946, negociations broke down completely, the Americans decided to
the case on trial.
z	ihe American War Crimes Prosecution Staff is now collecting
all evidence and information apertaining to the BUCHENWALD Case and would
greatly appreciate all documents we may have with any bearing on the case.
They further specify, that statements made by competent British odservers,
Members of FSrTiiment"and Members of the Board of Inquiry and other such
personages who were present in BUCHEN'ITALD‘ shortly after the 'Camp was
.liberated, would be accepted as evidence.
am anxious
4.
assistance from us in this case,
greatly appreciated.
that the Americans should have the maximum
would be

1	i’hs American War Crimes Prosecution Staff, which is np#
collecting all evidence and information apertaining oo the
BCGHSIf/iAlD Case, would greatly appreciate all documents we nay have
with any bearing on she case. They further specify that statement a
made by competent British observers, lumbers of Parliament and
Members of the Board of Inquiry and other such personages who were
present in BUOHEKWALB shortly after the camp was liberated, would
be accepted as evidence*.
2	Since the Americans took on this case this section has
so far transferred to their custody nearly 2C0 guards and admin-
istrative personnel of BTKJHSN AID, together with their camp docu-
ments. We have however no documents of the nature specified on
our files and it is assumed that you will take action in this
connection, with regard to any appropriate documents which you may
hold. .Meanwhile we axe signalling the Judge Advocate's Office
LONDON to ask for any statements of British observers etc which it
way be possible to obtain.

^ June 19U7
Dachau. June k--------In the midst of the second week of presenting the accus-
ed's case, the defense is putting together its side of the story of the notor-
ious Buchenwald concentration camp through witnesses who have denied that the
31 defendants committed brutalities and who related incidents of kindnesses.
Today a witness told the U.S. war crimes court he was treated by defen-
dant Edwin Katzen Ellenbogen outside normal hospital hours and that the pri-
soner-doctor dispensed drugs and medicines he purchased with his own money.
The witness declared he never saw or heard of Katz.en~Ellenbo.gen, j.ormer
American citizen, mistreating prisoners. Katzen-Ellenbogen is accused of caus-
ing the deaths of hundreds of fellow inmates through sadism and withholding
medical care.
Typical questions asked by the defense counsels of its own witnesses have
been: "Did you ever see or hear of mistreatment of prisoners a certain
defendant)?" — "Would you have heard of mistreatments if they have taken place.
iy.
To these questions, the witnesses have answered "no" and "yes", respective-
The defense is following its pre-announced course of defending only the
individuals accused, and not the system which was practiced by the Nazis.
Under cross-examination however, one witness, an ex-stenographer at a
sub-camp, told of typing an order involving the"liquidation" of certain, pri-
soners / Hermann Pister, former commanding officer of Buchenwald, admitted hav-
ing a shrunken head of a prisoner in a caoinet in his office.
Dachau, June 4---‘Two Germans were sentenced to death and three otners re-
ceived prison terms for their part in the murder of five unarmed and surren-
dered American airmen in U.S. war crimes trials here today.
In one case, Karl Eggert was convicted of participating 111 tne beating
and shooting of four fliers in the barracks of on eastern laborers'camp. Pre-
viously. three other participants had received death sonx.ences for me crime,
