Docteur J. Robert
April 9 tii, 1947.
I, the undersigned Robert, Jules, Joseph, medical
doctor, domiciled at Charlieu (Loire - France), decorated with
the "M^daille do la Resistance Frnncaise'', declare:
I was arrested on May l8,’l945* by the German Gestapo
and deported to Buchenwalu on December 14, 1943.
I hare known, at one of the outside commandos of 3u-
chenwald, at talbeck->veferlingen (Saxony) Hauptmann (Captain)
Schaaf who commanded this letter camp from January 1945 till
April 12, 1945.
This officer did not wear SS uniform and had a certaii
contempt for this arm.
As the physician of the commando I have very frequent-
ly drawn the attention of Hauptmann Schaaf to the insufficient
feeding of the detainees. Re did everything in his power to re-
medy thi state of affairs without, however, succeeding therein
Particularly I have seen him supplicate the management of the
mines by telephone to ameliorate the mode of living of the de-
tainees .
3 an assistant he haa an SC-bcharfuhrer and Schaaf
had constantly to check the brutalities of this f.C.O. I have
never seen Hauptmann Schaaf hit a detainee.
'.'hen an SS-soldier had committed a very grave act of
brutality towards one of th our fellow-inmates Hauptmann Schnuf
to whom I had eompicineu about this reprimanded the Su—culprit
severely in ray presence.
During the days preceding the liberation of the camp
by "mericsn troops Hauptmann Rchaaf had received the order vo
conduct his c np to Hamburg.by road. Those lingering, behi'
to be executed. Furthermore, by express order of Himmler
tainee vans to fall into Allied hands alive. Hauptmann be
hesitated for a long time between his duty and his huma
ments. At the end, thanks to him, the camp stayed on th
and was liberated by the '.mericam troops without bloods
In my spirit and conscience I consider that B
Schaaf has done everything in his power at the camp of
iVeferlingen to consider the detainees as prisoners of wf
has, by this fact, saved a considerable number of human
Not knowing, at the moment, the situation of
mann Schaaf, I am making this declaration purely in r
of justice.
G harlieu, Apri1 9 th, 19 4

At last something about the political views of Stephan t
Schaaf. It Was mentioned at the'beg Inning already that he was I
no member of the FSDAP, But Schaaf was a clear opponent of ;
the national-socialist ideology, he wds strictly catholic and\
as a result o/ his reserved and timid character, he was strtca
ly~ opposed to violence. In this connection he often declared
towards the family of Kasssrra that the control of trains wiM
the railway service which chiefly aimed at the discovery of
deserters wasdisgusting and loathsome for him. Be even spoke
of a mental affection by this service. Hispersonal decency
is proved by this behaviour towards the Kasserras.
Stephan Schaaf was an export merchant to England. Several
Statements stress the fact that Schaaf has always been pro-
Enol ish and that he even had reflected upon marrying an Eng-
lish lady and to move to England for ever. Is reliable proof
for this fact I have an English character of renown on hand
dated 14.5.1947, issued by the director Mr. H.L.Seaal. In the
firm of J.Segal Ltd.,55, Farrington Road,London, beside of
German declarations. .Mr. E.C.J.Segal declares his willingness
therein to procure further and more detailed information
about Schaaf to the British Military Government Authorities.
’ My general impre ssion of Captain Schaaf is that n4T reproa-
ches can be raised against him. Be aould not refuse the mili-
tary order as an officer to do service in a KZ camp} and it
did not contain anything opposed to human dignity as an order.
He used his service,however, to bring a bit humaneness also in-
to the KZ -distress. And at the end of the war, when the
marching-order appeared criminal to him he did not obey to it
and saved the life of several hundred human beings so. I there
for believe that I am able to carry the responsibility if I
propose to the British authorities' to kindly consider the soon
discharge of Captain Bchaaf. At the same time I should regard
is only as just if the denouncers should be called to account
as strictly as possible, they being criminal at that now al-
ready.

I, the undersigned KOMMEE, Charles, chief of the forester
service of the Treves District, declare:
On April 4, 1944, I was arrested by the German GESTAPO and
deported to BUGHEN AAID in July 1944 where I was affected with the
outside commando of v.EFfcRiIIGEi: (Saxony'' working in the salt mines.
From January 1945 until the liberation in April 1945 tne officer in
charge of this commando was Haupttimnn (Captain) CCH" ' I1 .
At the arrival of Hauptmann SCHAAF I was interpreter of the
commando and, in this capacity, in daily contact with SCHAAF. I there-
fore know him particularly well. Hauptmann SCHAAF never wore SS-anx-
form and never failed to remark at every pccasion that he was an oi
ficer of the wehrnaacht (Army). During the whole period of his oexng
in charge of” the commando his attitude towards the detainees has al-
ways been extremely correct, and he has done his best to ease their
lot. It is thanks to him that his assistant, an SC-Gcharflihrer whose
n^me I have forgotten, did not carry out the ili—trertment which he
announced daily, and I have often heard this scharfiihrei ui>ter the
words:"It is a'pitty I cannot do as I wish - otherwise I should have
done you in long ago". All the detainees knew perfectly well that
Hauptmann SCHAAF checked this ScharftLhrer with all possible means.
This officer also did everything in his power to induce the manage-
ment of the mines to amelioJBffite the lot of the commando - unluckily
without suscess. During the days preceding the liberation, at the
beginning of April, Hauptmann SCHAAF had received oraers to evacuate
the commando on foot towards Hamburg. As among the 500 men of the
commando about half were unable to march, I together with the physiv*
cian of the commando approached SCHAAF in order to avoid the execut-
ion of this order. After some hesitation Hauptmann SCHAAF consented
to leave the men where they were. The folio ing day a fresh formal
order to evacuate was reoslved, and for the second time Hauptmann
SCHAAF took it upon himself not to execute the order. In this manner
many human lives -were saved, and it is no exaggeration to say that
one can estimate the number of detainees who would have perished if
Hauptmann SCHAAF had carried out the order given him to be 250 at
the very least.
At the moment: of the approach of the American troops tvup ■> •
mann SCHAAF withdrew his men supervising the commando in perfect or-
der. and no ill-treatment whatever of the detainees uook place, 1
therefore consider that Hauptmann SCHAAF has done everything in his
cower to treat the internees under his command humanely and that no
reproach can be made to him for having been the commandant of a com-
mando of detainees for he advantageously held a position which, had
it been held by a. member of the SC would have resulted in the de- j
struction of the lives af a large number of men who, thanks to oUiy ..
have regained their native lands.
